16	COG2020_parser_usage = '''
17	===================================== COG2020 example commands =====================================
18	
19	# Dependencies
20	module load blast+
21	module load diamond
22	
23	# annotate protein sequences
24	BioSAK COG2020 -m P -t 6 -db_dir path/to/your/COG_db_dir -i genes.faa 
25	BioSAK COG2020 -m P -t 6 -db_dir path/to/your/COG_db_dir -i faa_files -x faa -d depth_files
26	
27	# annotate DNA sequences (ORFs)
28	BioSAK COG2020 -m N -t 6 -db_dir path/to/your/COG_db_dir -i genes.ffn -d gene.depth
29	BioSAK COG2020 -m N -t 6 -db_dir path/to/your/COG_db_dir -i ffn_files -x ffn
30	
31	# Prepare DB files (version 2020):
32	cd path/to/your/COG_db_dir
33	wget https://ftp.ncbi.nih.gov/pub/COG/COG2020/data/cog-20.fa.gz
34	wget https://ftp.ncbi.nih.gov/pub/COG/COG2020/data/cog-20.cog.csv
35	wget https://ftp.ncbi.nih.gov/pub/COG/COG2020/data/cog-20.def.tab
36	wget https://ftp.ncbi.nih.gov/pub/COG/COG2020/data/fun-20.tab
37	wget https://ftp.ncbi.nih.gov/pub/COG/COG2020/data/Readme.2020-11-25.txt
38	gunzip cog-20.fa.gz
39	makeblastdb -in cog-20.fa -dbtype prot -parse_seqids -logfile cog-20.fa.log
40	diamond makedb --in cog-20.fa --db cog-20.fa.dmnd --quiet
41	
42	# How it works:
43	1. COG2020 module uses Blast+/Diamond to get the best hits of query genes in the database 
44	   with users defined e-value cutoff (default 0.001).
45	2. The TotalDepth of a COG id/category is obtained by summing up the depth of all genes assigned to it.
46	3. The percentage of GeneNumber/TotalDepth of genes assigned to a COG is calculated by dividing them 
47	   by the total number/depth of genes with COG assignment (default) or all query genes in a file (if "-pct_by_all" specified). 
48	
49	# Note!!!
50	If you run COG2020 for multiple files in a batch manner and want to have their depth info incorporated into the results, 
51	you need to provide a folder containing individual depth file for each of your input sequence file.
52	Name of the depth file needs to be exactly the same as its corresponding sequence file, except the extension is ".depth".
53	
54	# Depth file format (one gene per line, tab separated)
55	gene_1	30
56	gene_2	10.58
57	
58	====================================================================================================
59	'''

15	KEGG_parser_usage = '''
16	======================================== KEGG example commands =======================================
17	
18	# Dependencies: blast+ or diamond
19	
20	# annotation with NCBI blastp (default, for small dataset)
21	BioSAK KEGG -db_dir path/to/your/KEGG_db_dir -t 6 -seq_in input.faa -d input.depth
22	
23	# annotation with Diamond blastp (for big dataset)
24	BioSAK KEGG -db_dir path/to/your/KEGG_db_dir -t 12 -seq_in faa_folder -x faa -d depth_files -diamond
25	
26	# get summary for BlastKOALA/GhostKOALA produced results
27	BioSAK KEGG -db_dir path/to/your/KEGG_db_dir -t 9 -ko_in user_ko.txt
28	BioSAK KEGG -db_dir path/to/your/KEGG_db_dir -t 9 -ko_in user_ko_folder -x txt
29	
30	# Prepare DB files, you need to have the following three files in your KEGG_db_dir:
31	1. Sequence file, only needed for "-seq_in" mode, DECOMPRESS and RENAME it to kegg_db_seq.fasta
32	   e.g. prokaryotes.pep.gz (https://www.kegg.jp/kegg/download/Readme/README.fasta)
33	2. seq2ko file, only needed for "-seq_in" mode, DECOMPRESS and RENAME it to kegg_db_seq2ko.txt
34	   e.g. prokaryotes.dat.gz (https://www.kegg.jp/kegg/download/Readme/README.fasta)
35	3. ko00001.keg
36	   https://www.genome.jp/kegg-bin/download_htext?htext=ko00001&format=htext&filedir=
37	
38	# seq2ko file format(tab separated)
39	aaa:Acav_4596	K05375
40	zpr:ZPR_0691	K21572
41	
42	# How it works:
43	1. KEGG module uses Blast+/Diamond to get the best hits of query genes in the database with user defined e-value cutoff (default 0.001).
44	2. The TotalDepth of a KO is calculated by summing up the depth of all genes assigned to it.
45	3. The percentage of GeneNumber/TotalDepth of genes assigned to a KO is calculated by dividing them 
46	   by the total number/depth of genes with KO assignment (default) or by all genes in a genome ("-pct_by_all"). 
47	
48	# Note!!!
49	1. If you run KEGG annotation for multiple files in a batch manner and want to have their depth info incorporated into the results, 
50	   you need to provide a folder containing individual depth files for each of your input sequence file.
51	   Name of the depth file needs to be exactly the same as its corresponding sequence file, except the extension which is ".depth".
52	2. Diamond requires quite a lot of memory for sequence comparison, especially for huge db file (e.g. KEGG db).
53	   Remember to request sufficient memory (e.g. 90 or 120gb) in your job script and specify a small number (e.g. -t 6) 
54	   of jobs executing in parallel. Otherwise, you may see some of your query genomes with no gene been annotated.
55	
56	# Depth file format (one gene per line, tab separated)
57	gene_1	30
58	gene_2	10.58
59	
60	# To do:
61	1. level C stats: separate stats for Pathway, Brite and the rests
62	
63	======================================================================================================
64	'''
65

26	# How it works:

28	2. The TotalDepth of a CAZy family is calculated by summing up the depth of all genes assigned to it.
29	3. The percentage of GeneNumber/TotalDepth of genes assigned to a CAZy family is calculated by dividing it 
30	   by the summation of GeneNumber/TotalDepth of all identified CAZy families. 
31	
32	# Note!!!

38	gene_1	30
39	gene_2	10.58
40	
41	========================================================================================================================
42	'''

9	enrich_usage = '''
10	======================================= enrich example commands =======================================
11	
12	BioSAK enrich -i annotation_files -x txt -g grouping.txt -o output_dir
13	BioSAK enrich -i annotation_files -x txt -g grouping.txt -o output_dir -bc
14	
15	# Note:
16	1. The number of genome groups has to be TWO!!!
17	2. Group name should NOT be 1 and 0. use some alphabet or words instead.
18	
19	# Example input files: https://github.com/songweizhi/BioSAK/tree/master/demo_data/enrich
20	
21	# please refers to https://doi.org/10.1038/s41396-020-00815-8 for how it works:
22	Functions that are enriched in the genomes in either group are identified using MannWhitney U 
23	tests followed by a Bonferroni correction with a p value cut-off of 0.05 being considered 
24	significant. Only significantly different functions with greater than, by default, 2-fold mean 
25	differences are considered to be enriched. Functions detected only in the genomes from one group 
26	type are considered to be enriched if they existed in at least 50 percent of the genomes in the group.
27	
28	=======================================================================================================
29	'''

23

26
